Key Findings

  • Analog benchmark: Selected analogs: NCT02633163, NCT02847598, NCT05531565. Fewer than five selected analog trials were available, limiting benchmark stability.
  • Executive synopsis: Draft strategy brief for Envudeucitinib in SLE. The target registry record is NCT05966480, PHASE2, and this artifact requires human review before protocol use.
  • Endpoint strategy: Draft endpoint strategy should align with analog endpoint-family frequencies and the target trial primary endpoint family: response. Statistical review is required before endpoint hierarchy or powering assumptions are used.
  • Safety monitoring: Safety monitoring should incorporate openFDA label context when available and safety exclusion themes from analog trial eligibility criteria. This is a review prompt, not a final safety plan.
  • Reviewer critique: Fewer than five selected analog trials were available, limiting benchmark stability.

  • PubMed retrieval failed: PubMedError.

Grade E indicates no current or previous disease activity.         "eligibility_criteria": "Key Inclusion Criteria:\n\nPart A:\n\n1. Diagnosis of systemic lupus erythematosus (SLE) fulfilling at least 4 out of 11 of the 1997 revised American College of Rheumatology (ACR) classification criteria for SLE along with active skin manifestations and joint involvement.\n2. At least 4 tender joints and at least 4 swollen joints with at least 4 of the swollen joints in the proximal interphalangeal (PIP) joints, metacarpophalangeal (MCP) joints and/or wrist.\n3. Demonstrate at least one sign of active lupus skin disease, including acute cutaneous lupus erythematosus (ACLE), subacute cutaneous lupus erythematosus (SCLE), and/or chronic cutaneous lupus erythematosus (CCLE) (e.g., discoid lupus erythematosus (DLE)), with skin activity defined by SLE Disease Activity Index 2000 (SLEDAI-2K) at the time of Screening and randomization.\n\nPart B:\n\n1\\. Active skin manifestations Cutaneous Lupus Erythematosus Disease Area and Severity Index Activity (CLASI-A) ≥8)) and a diagnosis of cutaneous lupus erythematosus (CLE) that has been histologically confirmed (in the past or at Screening), with or without SLE manifestations.\n\nKey Exclusion Criteria:\n\n1. Active lupus nephritis or moderate-to-severe or chronic kidney disease.\n2. Any active skin conditions other than CLE that may interfere with the study (e.g., psoriasis, non-LE skin lupus, drug-induced lupus).\n3. History of chronic, recurrent (3 or more of the same type of infection in a 12-month period), or recent serious infection (e.g., pneumonia, septicemia, herpes zoster) as determined by the Investigator and requiring anti-infective treatment within 12 weeks prior to Screening.\n4. Use of immunosuppressive or disease-modifying treatments for SLE or CLE that were initiated less than 12 weeks prior to Randomization.\n\nNOTE: Other protocol defined Inclusion/Exclusion criteria may apply",

      "eligibility_criteria": "Inclusion Criteria:\n\nPatients with 6 or more months of SLE according to the 2019 EULAR/ACR criteria, have positive autoantibodies or low complement at screening, and have active SLE as measured by SLEDAI-2K of 6 or more, or 4 or more if joint involvement is present.\n\nPatients need to be on treatment which can be:\n\n* A stable dose of oral corticosteroid (≤40 mg/day prednisone or equivalent) for a minimum of 2 weeks prior to signing of the informed consent form (ICF) at the Screening Visit. Examples include severe fibromyalgia, severe osteoarthritis and severe cardiorespiratory diseases.\n* Active severe or unstable neuropsychiatric SLE including, but not limited to the following: aseptic meningitis; cerebral vasculitis; myelopathy; demyelination syndromes (ascending or transverse myelitis, acute inflammatory demyelinating polyradiculopathy); acute confusional state; impaired level of consciousness; psychosis; acute stroke or stroke syndrome; cranial neuropathy; new seizures; cerebellar ataxia; and mononeuritis multiplex.\n\n  * That would make the patient unable to fully understand the ICF, or\n  * Where, in the opinion of the Principal Investigator, protocol-specified SOC is insufficient and utilization of a more aggressive therapeutic approach not permitted in the protocol, is indicated\n* Known history of a primary immunodeficiency or an underlying condition such as HIV infection or splenectomy that predisposes the patient to infection\n* Currently active, clinically significant infection of any kind\n* Clinically significant chronic infection (eg, osteomyelitis, bronchiectasis) within 8 weeks prior to signing the ICF (chronic fungal nail infections are allowed)\n* Any infection requiring hospitalization or treatment with IV anti-infectives not completed at least 4 weeks prior to signing the ICF\n* Any infection requiring oral anti-infectives (including antivirals) within 2 weeks prior to Day 1\n* Any severe herpes infection at any time prior to Week 0 (Day 1), including, but not limited to, disseminated herpes (ever), herpes encephalitis (ever), recurrent herpes zoster (defined as 2 episodes within 2 years), or ophthalmic herpes (ever)\n\n  * Active herpes zoster infection within 12 weeks of prior to signing the ICF\n  * Active herpes simplex virus within 4 weeks of Day 1\n* Other protocol-defined inclusion/exclusion criteria apply",

              "time_frame": "Baseline to Week 24",
              "description": "The SLEDAI-2K is a reliable, valid, simple, 1-page activity index that measures disease activity and records features of active lupus as present or not. It uses a weighted checklist to assign a numeric score based on the presence or absence of 24 symptoms at the time of assessment or during the previous 28 days. Each symptom present is assigned between 1 and up to 8 points based on its usual clinical importance, yielding a total score that ranges from 0 points (no symptoms) to 105 points (presence of all defined symptoms), where higher scores representing increased disease activity.",

              "time_frame": "Week 24",
              "description": "No new organ system affected, as defined by no new British Isles Lupus Activity Group (BILAG)-2004 A and no more than one new BILAG-2004 B. The BILAG-2004 index categorizes disease activity in each organ system into five different levels from A to E. Grade A represents very active disease, Grade B represents moderate disease activity, Grade C indicates mild stable disease, and grade D implies no disease activity, but suggests the organ system had previously been affected. Grade E indicates no current or previous disease activity. A score is applied to each grade of each organ system using coding scheme of A=12, B=8, C=1, and D/E=0 and is summarized as a total score ranging 0-108. Higher scores indicate more severe disease activity.",

          "eligibility_criteria": "Key Inclusion Criteria:\n\nPart A:\n\n1. Diagnosis of systemic lupus erythematosus (SLE) fulfilling at least 4 out of 11 of the 1997 revised American College of Rheumatology (ACR) classification criteria for SLE along with active skin manifestations and joint involvement.\n2. Active lupus nephritis or moderate-to-severe or chronic kidney disease.\n2. Any active skin conditions other than CLE that may interfere with the study (e.g., psoriasis, non-LE skin lupus, drug-induced lupus).\n3. History of chronic, recurrent (3 or more of the same type of infection in a 12-month period), or recent serious infection (e.g., pneumonia, septicemia, herpes zoster) as determined by the Investigator and requiring anti-infective treatment within 12 weeks prior to Screening.\n4. Use of immunosuppressive or disease-modifying treatments for SLE or CLE that were initiated less than 12 weeks prior to Randomization.\n\nNOTE: Other protocol defined Inclusion/Exclusion criteria may apply",
